- **Ō£ģ RESOLVED ŌĆö Cloudflare Workers AI now drives the coding tool loop; `@cf/qwen/qwen3-30b-a3b-fp8` is a paid coder ahead of Claude** (2026-06-14). The `cloudflare` vendor now translates tools both ways: OpenAI `[{type:'function',function:{ŌĆ”}}]` ŌåÆ Cloudflare native `[{name,description,parameters}]` on the request (`buildBody`/`toCloudflareTools`; `tool_choice` dropped ŌĆö native /ai/run has none), and Cloudflare `result.tool_calls` (`{name,arguments}`, no id, object args) ŌåÆ OpenAI `choices[0].message.tool_calls` (synthesized id, JSON-stringified args) on the response (`adaptCloudflareResponse`), so `parseLlmChoice` + the multi-turn coding loop work. `@cf/qwen/qwen3-30b-a3b-fp8` is marked tool-capable, added to `CODING_MODEL_POOL` (paid-coder section ŌåÆ shows in the Pro picker, not Free) and inserted into `CODING_PREMIUM_FALLBACK_MODELS` **before** every Claude entry (vendor-diverse from both OpenRouter and Anthropic; no-key-skips when the Cloudflare token/account aren't bound). `@cf/google/gemma-4-26b-a4b-it` stays a general PRO-pool chat model (not a coder). Covered by new cases in `LlmProxyService.codingPool.test.ts` (api llm suite green).

- **Ō£ģ RESOLVED ŌĆö Learned model routing (PRD 13) implemented end-to-end across all 3 phases (capture ŌåÆ analyze + route ŌåÆ client SSM recall bias)** (2026-06-15). Built on the existing capture substrate (no parallel "model used" store): (1) **Taxonomy** ŌĆö closed `ACTION_TYPES` enum in `api/src/application/llm/actionTypes.ts` (mirrored to `frontend/src/lib/builderforceApi.ts`), the single source for classifier/router/scorer/analytics/UI; `learnedRoutingEnabled` kill switch (`LEARNED_ROUTING_ENABLED`, default on). (2) **Classifier** ŌĆö `classifyTask.ts` runs ONCE per task on the FREE pool (strict json_schema) and caches on `tasks.action_type` (+ `action_type_confidence`, migration 0197); `resolveLearnedRoutingInputs` in `cloudAgentEngine` classifies-or-reuses on the first tick, best-effort ŌåÆ `other`. (3) **Outcome scorer** ŌĆö `scoreRunOutcome.ts` writes one `run_model_outcomes` row (migration 0198, unique `execution_id`) per terminal cloud run via the pure `computeOutcomeScore` (D3: merge 0.5 + green-CI 0.2 + no-degradation 0.15 + efficiency 0.15, approval pins completion, failed/cancelled = 0); wired at every terminal chokepoint (DO `cleanup`, Worker `runCloudExecution` ├Ś3, container `finalize`/`fail`), idempotent + best-effort. (4) **Routing table** ŌĆö `routingTable.ts`: a derived `routing:<scope>` KV blob (projectŌåÆtenantŌåÆglobal) maintained by incremental Welford RMW on each outcome (no table scan), read by the router AND the analytics endpoint via `getOrSetCached`; cold miss reconciles from a single grouped SQL. (5) **Router** ŌĆö pure `rankModelsForAction` reorders `codingModelsForPlan` by avgScore (+ MIN_SAMPLES=8 floor, cost tie-break, optional bias); `pickCloudModel` gains learned opts (free-plan gate + explicit-pin byte-for-byte unchanged; soft seed = `ranked[0]`); `model.select` explains the choice. (6) **Analytics** ŌĆö `GET /llm/v1/model-analytics` + `ModelRoutingAnalytics` panel (Workforce ŌåÆ LLM tab). (7) **Client SSM bias** ŌĆö `frontend/src/lib/modelRecallBias.ts` (WebGPU+IndexedDB-gated embedŌåÆkNNŌåÆbias), seeded via `GET /llm/v1/recall-seed`, threaded interactive-launch-only through `parseRoutingBias` ŌåÆ `pickCloudModel`. Tests: `actionTypes`, `classifyTask`, `routingTable`, `scoreRunOutcome`, extended `codingPool`, `modelRecallBias` (api 940 + frontend 247 green). **Residuals (deferred):** (a) **on-prem/host runs aren't routed** by this (cloud-only phase 1 per PRD ┬¦10) ŌĆö host picks its own model; (b) **no scheduled reconcile cron** ŌĆö the blob reconciles only on a cold-cache read, so a lost-update race from concurrent same-bucket terminals self-heals only on the next KV eviction, not on a timer (add a cron calling `reconcileRoutingTable` per active scope); (c) **the SSM embedding is a deterministic feature-hash, not a real MambaKit/SSMjs WebGPU SSM embedding** ŌĆö the `embedTask` seam is in place but the per-codebase `model.bin` weights aren't pushed from builderforce.ai yet (drop-in swap behind the same signature); (d) **recall memory is pull-seeded** (`/recall-seed`), not pushed live over the execution-steering WS as PRD ┬¦6.6 envisions (cross-device freshness lags until the next mount); (e) **the container `llm` op doesn't apply learned routing** (only the DO/Worker `runCloudToolLoop` does) ŌĆö fine while the container falls back to DO, but a parity gap if the long-lived container surface ships. Unblocks: task-aware model routing + per-codebase learned preferences.

- **Superseded (now resolved) ŌĆö Learned model routing design notes.** (2026-06-14). Every cloud run's **resolved model** is already captured per task/project (`recordCloudUsage` ŌåÆ `llm_usage_log.model` + attribution `{cloudAgentRef, executionId, taskId, projectId}`; plus `model.select`/`coding_model_degraded` timeline events) ŌĆö so the "which model ran" substrate exists. Missing is the learned-routing loop the operator wants: (1) **action-type labels** ŌĆö classify each task into an action type (`sql`, `frontend`, `refactor`, `bugfix`, ŌĆ”) so runs group by type; proposed first step is a cheap **first-pass FREE-model classifier** that tags the task before the run (decision: add a per-run classifier call? store the label where ŌĆö a `task_action_type` column / a `run_labels` table?). (2) **outcome signal** ŌĆö define "worked best" (PR merged? green CI? human approval? steps-to-done? token cost?) and join it to `(action_type, model)` so analytics can rank models per type ("Google/Gemini best at SQL"). (3) **routing** ŌĆö feed the ranking back into selection (extend `pickCloudModel`/`codingModelsForPlan` with an action-typeŌåÆmodel preference), with **SSM/Samba memory** (MambaKit/SSMjs hippocampus ŌĆö see the SSM Hippocampus loop) as the per-codebase recall layer that learns which models work best for THIS repo over time. Design-level subsystem spanning api + SSMjs/MambaKit; **not** built this pass to avoid a dead/half-wired routing seam. Blockers needing an explicit decision: the "best" outcome metric, whether to add a first-pass classifier call on every run (cost), and the SSM integration surface. Unblocks: task-aware model routing + per-codebase learned model preferences.

- **Ō£ģ RESOLVED ŌĆö a failing CI build on the agent's PR branch now surfaces WHY on the ticket and feeds the reason back to the agent (pre-merge), not just post-merge** (2026-06-14). An agent could mark a task "complete" while the build on its `builderforce/task-<id>` branch was red, and the failure reason was invisible on the ticket ŌĆö the pre-merge CI path (`ingestRepoCiEvent.ingestPreMergeEvent`) only recorded a bare `ci.<event>` telemetry ping with the outcome + URL: it never fetched the failing jobs/steps, never persisted a build status/reason on the PR row, and never dispatched an auto-fix (only the POST-merge path did). Fixed by making both phases symmetric through one shared `applyBuildOutcome` helper: on a pre-merge failure it (1) **fetches the failing jobs/steps** via the existing `fetchBuildError`, (2) **persists `build_status` + the reason on the open PR row** (new `build_error` column, migration 0196; new `findOpenPullRequestByTask`; `setPullRequestBuildStatus` extended to write/clear the reason), (3) records a prominent `build.result` timeline event, and (4) **dispatches an auto-fix run** (same per-task attempt cap / loop-guard) carrying a phase-tagged `remediation` block so the cloud agent's prompt is framed as "the CI build on your PR branch FAILED ŌĆö fix it before merge" (`parseRemediation` + `cloudAgentEngine` prompt are now `phase`-aware). Auto-fix on the PR branch is gated to authoritative `workflow_run` conclusions (a `runId`) so the many per-check events on a branch don't each burn an attempt. UI: `PullRequestPanel` now renders a `BuildStatus` block (status badge + the failing-jobs/steps reason in a scrollable `<pre>` + auto-fix note) for the OPEN PR too, and polls while pre-merge build is pending. Covered by 5 new pre-merge cases in `ingestRepoCiEvent.test.ts` + a pre-merge-phase case in `cloudDispatch.test.ts` (api ci+runtime suites green); frontend `tsc` clean. Sibling to the runtime-crash-reason work above ŌĆö this is the CI-build-failure counterpart.

- **A failing PR-branch build is surfaced on the Pull Request tab, but not yet as a ticket/execution-chip badge** (2026-06-14). The build status + reason now persist on the PR row and render in `PullRequestPanel` (the ticket's "Pull Request" tab) and the run's Logs/Timeline. What's missing is a higher-altitude signal: the execution chip (`#64 ┬Ę cancelled`) and the task card don't show a "build failing" badge, so a buyer scanning the executions list still can't tell at a glance that a "completed" run shipped a red build. Deferred: derive a `buildStatus` badge on `AgentExecutionPanel`'s execution chips + the task card from the linked PR row (the data is already there via `getTaskPullRequest`). Unblocks: red-build visibility without opening the PR tab.

- **Task-PRD content ŌĆö fence-wrap normalized at the render path + on new writes; only the historical backfill remains.** LLM-drafted PRDs sometimes arrive wrapped in a whole-document ` ```markdown ` fence, which `ChatMessageContent` rendered as one raw "MARKDOWN" code box in the task-details PRD tab instead of formatted prose. Closed two ways: (1) **render-time** ŌĆö `TaskPrdTab` now runs `unwrapMarkdownFence` (the generalized ex-`unwrapLegalMarkdown` util) and adds a `Preview | RAW` `ViewToggle` (panel + fullscreen), so existing rows display correctly; (2) **on WRITE** ŌĆö `draftTaskPrd` (`api/.../prd/taskPrd.ts`) strips the fence via new `stripPrdMarkdownFence` before persisting, so freshly generated PRDs are stored clean for every consumer (render/export/repo-commit/Copy). **Residual (operator):** a one-off backfill of `specs.prd` rows persisted before this change ŌĆö until then the render-time unwrap stays the safety net (can't be retired). No code change available for the backfill without live-DB access. Mirrors the legal-doc normalization gap above.

- **Ō£ģ RESOLVED ŌĆö backplanes now report WHY they crashed, and self-heal is unified across every detector** (2026-06-14). Three fixes shipped together: (1) **Crash reasons surfaced** ŌĆö the container image (`api/container/server.mjs`) reports a caught loop crash on a dedicated `fail` container-op (not `finalize`, which implied an orderly finish), and `AgentContainerDO.onError` (which only `console.error`'d before) now attributes a hard container death (OOM / evict / unbootable image) to its execution and reports the real error; `CloudRunnerDO` already reported its `errorMessage`. New `cloudCrashReason()` carries the actual message to the timeline. (2) **One self-heal** ŌĆö `api/src/application/runtime/cloudSelfHeal.ts` is the single once-only "re-queue on the durable executor, else fail with the real reason" path, shared by the cron reaper (`staleExecutionReaper`, refactored onto shared `isSelfHealEligible`/`buildDurableStartBody`/`dispatchDurableStart`), the container `fail` op + `onError` (`handleCloudRunCrash`), AND the read-path repair `RuntimeService.reapIfOrphaned` (new `onCloudOrphan` DI callback wired in `index.ts`). This closes the race that bit execution #62: the read path used to permanently fail a crashed run before the cron could retry it; now it self-heals first. (3) **Surface-aware orphan reason** ŌĆö `cloudOrphanReason` no longer claims a "~30s serverless limit / downgrade to durable" on a container/durable run that ran past the wall. Covered by `cloudSelfHeal.test.ts` (11) + reaper/orphan-reason tests; full api suite green (879).
- **Container hard-death (`onError`) self-heal can't push a LIVE WebSocket event** (2026-06-14). `AgentContainerDO.onError` runs in the container DO's isolate, where the per-run WS subscriber map and the `executionBoardSink` (SESSION_ROOM fan-out) are not registered (they're wired per request isolate). So when a container crash self-heals or fails via `handleCloudRunCrash`, the failure/requeue is persisted + lands a `run.failed`/`runtime.crash` timeline row, but live subscribers only see it on the next read-path reconciliation poll (a few seconds), not instantly ŌĆö same latency as today's orphan reaps. The container `fail` op path (in the Worker request isolate) DOES push live. Deferred: have `handleCloudRunCrash` emit through a cross-isolate notifier (e.g. always via the SESSION_ROOM DO) so a DO-isolate crash pushes instantly too. Unblocks: real-time crash surfacing regardless of which isolate detected it.
- **Ō£ģ RESOLVED ŌĆö a cloud coding run can no longer fall through to a non-coder backstop; it floors onto paid coders or fails honestly** (2026-06-14). Root cause: a `codingOnly` proxy restricted its *primary* pool to `CODING_MODEL_POOL` but still appended the general non-coder premium-fallback chain (`PREMIUM_FALLBACK_MODELS` ŌåÆ `googleai/gemini-2.5-flash`) inline, and its backstop chain ended in the non-coder `GUARANTEED_BACKSTOP_MODEL` ŌĆö so an exhausted coding cascade resolved onto a generalist that loops on search and ships no edits (execution #62: ~77s, one orphan file, no wiring). Fixed in `LlmProxyService`: (1) new `CODING_PREMIUM_FALLBACK_MODELS` (paid coders ŌĆö DeepSeek/Xiaomi/Anthropic, vendor-diverse, cheapest-first) is the appended fallback for `codingOnly` proxies via a new `codingOnly` option on the service + the `premiumFallback` getter; (2) `CODING_BACKSTOP_MODELS` is now coders-only (the gemini last-resort removed) ŌĆö if every paid coder is also down the run surfaces `cascade_exhausted` (an honest failure beats a weak-model run that fakes progress); (3) `PAID_OVERFLOW_MODELS` metering kept precise ŌĆö only the cheap `CHEAPEST_PAID_CODER` is flagged by id (the flagship Pro plan coders are metered as overflow only via the explicit backstop `paidOverflow=true` flag, so a Pro tenant's legit plan usage isn't mis-metered). `coding_model_degraded` telemetry stays as a safety net for an explicit non-coder pin. Covered by new/updated tests in `LlmProxyService.backstop.test.ts`, `LlmProxyService.overflow.test.ts`, `cloudAgentEngine.test.ts`, `cloudTelemetry.test.ts` (llm+runtime suites green: 295).
- **Lane agent's host `target` is not threaded into the dispatcher** (2026-06-14). `decideLaneAutoRun` returns the lane agent's `agentRef` + `model`; the dispatcher (`startDispatchedExecution`) resolves the on-prem host from a pin on the *task* (`tasks.assignedAgentHostId`). A swimlane agent that pins its own host `target` (a specific on-prem machine) does not yet propagate that into the run, so a lane can't direct its run to a particular machine ŌĆö host delivery only happens when the task itself is host-pinned. Unblocks: per-lane choice of which on-prem machine runs the stage. (The V2-on-host engine gate is now removed ŌĆö host delivery is no longer gated on engine; the on-prem host runtime runs the V2 Agent natively, and the run carries the agent's own model.)
- **Ō£ģ RESOLVED ŌĆö board drag into a staffed lane created the run but never fired the agent** (2026-06-15). Two compounding causes in the autonomous lane trigger (`taskRoutes.ts:maybeAutoRunOnLaneEntry`). (1) The trigger was deferred into `c.executionCtx.waitUntil(...)` and then, from inside that post-response continuation, the dispatcher (`startDispatchedExecution`) re-registered the executor kickoff via *another* `c.executionCtx.waitUntil(orchestrate())` ŌĆö registering work on an already-closed request context throws ("I/O on behalf of a different request"), which the trigger's `try/catch` swallowed, so `runtimeService.submit` created the `executions` row but `orchestrate()` never ran (run stuck, agent never started). Fixed by having `maybeAutoRunOnLaneEntry` COLLECT the dispatcher's deferred kickoff and `await Promise.allSettled(...)` it inside its own promise (we are already off the response path), so the single outer `waitUntil` registered *during* request handling keeps the whole chain ŌĆö kickoff included ŌĆö alive. (2) The idempotency guard used a raw `db.select` over `executions` in live statuses; a cloud run abandoned `RUNNING` by an evicted isolate is only reaped on READ, so a dead row blocked the lane's agent forever on any ticket that had run once before. Now reads through `runtimeService.listByTask` so orphans reap to FAILED first. Also consolidated the create + PATCH wiring into one route helper (`fireLaneAutoRun`) and dropped the per-call `waitUntil` lambda from the signature; the agent-advance path (`buildRuntimeService` `onLaneEntry`) reuses the same function. `tsc` clean.
- **Auto-run execution CREATION is not pushed over the project socket ŌĆö only poll-surfaced** (2026-06-15). The board/cards/lanes update live via `broadcastProjectChanged` (SESSION_ROOM) on task writes, and the lane drag itself pushes. But when the autonomous trigger submits the auto-run, neither `runtimeService.submit` nor `startDispatchedExecution` broadcasts to the project room ŌĆö only `notifyExecutionSubscribers` (the per-execution stream). So the freshly-queued run CHIP (e.g. "Bob ┬Ę pending") surfaces on the board's `useBoardLiveRuns` poll tick, not instantly over WS, despite the run-feed comment treating WS as primary and the poll as a dropped-socket backstop. Distinct from the container-crash WS gap above (that's failure surfacing; this is creation surfacing). Deferred: emit a `broadcastProjectChanged` (or a dedicated run-created event) at dispatch so the chip appears the instant the agent is queued. Unblocks: instant "agent picked it up" feedback on drag without waiting for the reconcile poll.
- **`ide_agents.engine` column + V1 engine values are vestigial post-V1-deletion** (2026-06-14). V1 is deleted in the cloud AND on the on-prem host (the agent-runtime engine registry's sole runner is `builderforce-v2`; any legacy `engine` value falls back to v2). The API dispatch path no longer branches on engine (the `!isV2` gate and the `cloudAgentTypeLabel` V1 branch are gone). The `ide_agents.engine` column is now effectively constant and any rows still holding `'builderforce-v1'` are inert (resolve/behave as v2). Deferred: a migration to normalize/drop the `engine` column. The engine *registry* DI seam is INTENTIONALLY kept (a future V3 registers the same way). Unblocks: schema/code clarity once the column is retired.
- **Autonomous lane runs bypass the execution governance approval gate** (2026-06-14). The manual `/api/runtime/executions` route runs `evaluateExecutionApprovalGate` (governance approval rules ŌĆö currently gates high/urgent priority tasks) before dispatch; the autonomous lane trigger (via `dispatchCloudRunForTask`) skips it. The lane's own `gate: 'human'` provides board-level human-in-the-loop, but tenant governance approval *rules* are not enforced on autonomously-triggered runs. NOT auto-bundled: applying it would make a high-priority task's autonomous run create an approval instead of running, a product decision (`evaluateExecutionApprovalGate` is currently route-private in `runtimeRoutes.ts` ŌĆö extract + share when adopted). Unblocks: consistent policy enforcement ŌĆö every agent run (manual or autonomous) honors the same approval rules.
- **Capability guardrail only enforces an explicitly-configured `required_capabilities`; there is no capability-aware *router*** (2026-06-14). `decideLaneAutoRun` now skips a lane agent whose resolved skills/personas don't cover the lane assignment's `required_capabilities` (`api/src/application/swimlane/laneAutoRun.ts` + the resolve+warn wiring in `taskRoutes.ts:maybeAutoRunOnLaneEntry`), which closes the "BA/PM/PO agent silently runs a coding task" hole **when a lane sets the field**. A lane with no `required_capabilities` configured still runs whatever agent is pinned (the exec #61 lane had none set). Deferred: (a) a real router that *scores* a task's inferred type (coding/docs/review) against each workforce agent's persona/skills and picks the best match rather than the first qualifying one (the AskUserQuestion "full capability-aware router" option), and (b) a sensible default requirement (e.g. infer `coding-agent` for a lane whose template writes code) so the guardrail protects un-configured lanes too. Unblocks: correct-by-default staffing without per-lane manual config.
- **`capability_mismatch` has no pre-execution timeline channel** (2026-06-14). When the guardrail skips a mis-staffed agent it emits a `console.warn` (Worker telemetry sink) only ŌĆö there is no `execution_id` yet (we are *refusing* to start a run), so it can't ride the existing `recordCloudToolEvent` ŌåÆ Observability timeline path. The mismatch is therefore diagnosable in logs but invisible on the board/timeline. Deferred: a lightweight pre-execution audit channel (e.g. a per-task `auto_run_skipped` audit event) surfaced on the task card so a lane that silently won't auto-run explains itself in-product. Unblocks: operators see *why* a ticket dropped into an auto lane didn't start.
- **`capabilities.load` telemetry conflates agent-pinned vs inherited artifacts** (2026-06-14). The cloud run resolves capabilities via `resolveArtifacts({tenantId, taskId, cloudAgentRef})` ŌĆö a UNION across tenant + project + task + agent scopes ŌĆö and the `capabilities.load` timeline event reports that union. So an agent whose own (`scope='agent'`) config is empty still shows personas/skills assigned tenant- or project-wide (this is why exec #61's "Kevin BA/PM/PO" appeared to have `code-creator`/`documentation-agent` it was never directly assigned). The new /workforce **Agent manifest** (`api/src/application/artifact/agentManifest.ts`) deliberately shows the agent-scoped set ONLY, which is the honest "what is pinned to THIS agent" view. Deferred: make `capabilities.load` label each artifact with its source scope (agent vs project vs tenant) so the timeline distinguishes pinned from inherited ŌĆö and reconsider whether tenant-wide persona assignments should silently apply to every agent at all. Unblocks: an operator can tell, from telemetry alone, what an agent itself carries vs what it merely inherited.
- **Moving a task across boards does not re-point `tasks.segment_id` to the target project's segment** (2026-06-14). `TaskService.moveTask` (now collision-safe re-keying) updates `project_id` + `key` but leaves `segment_id` pointing at the *source* project's segment. The `set_default_segment_id_via_project` trigger only fires `BEFORE INSERT`, and `segment_id` isn't modeled in the `Task` domain entity or written by `TaskRepository.update`, so a moved row keeps its old segment. Harmless for `single`-mode tenants (one shared default segment, so source and target segments are identical), but for a `segmented` tenant whose source/target projects live in different segments this leaves the task's segment stale ŌĆö a data-isolation drift. Deferred (T7 ŌĆö segment/isolation): on move, resolve the target project's `segment_id` and update the task to match (or add an `AFTER UPDATE OF project_id` trigger that re-derives it). Unblocks: correct per-segment attribution/erasure (DSR/GDPR cascade) for tasks that change boards in a segmented tenant.
- **A vendor-specific 400 inside the coding cascade can still suppress the paid coding backstop** (2026-06-14). `LlmProxyService.complete()` treats a primary cascade that ends in `outcome === 'request_error'` (every candidate returned 400/422) as "the caller's payload is malformed" and **skips** the guaranteed backstop (so it surfaces the schema diagnostic instead of double-billing a doomed retry). That assumption is wrong when the 400 is *vendor-specific* (e.g. Ollama's `"Value looks like objectŌĆ”"` on a tools payload that Anthropic/DeepSeek accept). The exec #61 trigger is now removed two ways ŌĆö Ollama is excluded from auto-routed pools and cloud coding runs cascade only within the curated coding pool (`codingOnly`), so a request-error finish is now unlikely ŌĆö but the short-circuit itself is unchanged. Deferred: fire the *coding* backstop (`CODING_BACKSTOP_MODELS`, a paid coder) even on `request_error`, since a paid coder is the most likely to accept a payload that quirky free vendors rejected. Unblocks: "a coding run always falls over to a paid coder" holds even in the all-400 edge.
- **`PATCH /api/approvals/:id` does not enforce the MANAGER+ role its own contract claims** (2026-06-14). The route's doc header says "tenant JWT, MANAGER+", but the handler (`approvalRoutes.ts`) only runs `authMiddleware` ŌĆö any authenticated tenant user can approve/reject/answer a request, including the new `task.execution` execution-approval gate (which, as of this pass, now *auto-starts the run* on approve via `dispatchCloudRunForTask`). So a non-manager can both clear the governance gate and trigger the (billable) run. Surfaced while wiring the inline `ApprovalResolveControl`; not fixed here because role-gating writes is a deliberate access-control change (need the canonical role check helper + a decision on which roles may approve which `actionType`s). Deferred (T7 ŌĆö governance): enforce role on the PATCH (and ideally scope by action type / approval rule). Unblocks: the execution-approval gate is real authorization, not an honor-system label. Note the inline approve UI already degrades safely ŌĆö a forbidden PATCH surfaces its error in the control ŌĆö so the only missing piece is the server-side role check.

### Ō£ģ Done / Resolved (53)

_Resolved/closed register items, grouped by the work they came from. Newest dates win; `git log` is the full audit trail._

#### ­¤¦Ā Brain conversation rendering (4)

- **Brain agent loop now survives Brain-initiated navigation ŌĆö FIXED 2026-06-14 (`brain-embedded/src/brainRunStore.ts` (new) + `useBrainConversation.ts` + `frontend/.../PlatformActionsBridge.tsx`, `BrainPanel.tsx`).** When the Brain navigated the user (`navigate_to`/`open_project`) off the full-page `/brainstorm` or the IDE-embedded Brain, the route-scoped panel unmounted mid-run: the loop's state (rich transcript, trace, streaming delta, confirm resolver) lived in that component's refs, so the run was orphaned, the freshly mounted instance lost all grounding, and ŌĆö worst ŌĆö it re-answered the trailing user message, spawning a **second concurrent loop** (duplicate writes). Fix: the tool-loop is hoisted into a module-level singleton (`brainRunStore`) keyed by chatId, **single-flight** per chat; any mounted Brain instance subscribes to the same run cell and renders the live run, and a second instance that tries to start the same chat is a no-op. The human-in-the-loop confirm gate also moved into the store, so a navigation that swaps which panel is mounted can still resolve a pending confirmation. `PlatformActionsBridge` force-opens the floating drawer on Brain-initiated nav and `BrainPanel` (page variant) mirrors its active chat into `BrainContext`, so the drawer resumes the exact conversation. Residual (memory eviction) logged above.
- **Brain drawer still closed on navigation paths the 2026-06-14 fix didn't cover ŌĆö FIXED 2026-06-16 (`brain-embedded/src/BrainContext.tsx` + `frontend/src/components/ChatMessageContent.tsx`).** The above fix kept the Brain open only across its own `navigate_to`/`open_project` tool calls (which `router.push` + `setOpen(true)`). Two other navigation paths still silently closed the drawer: (1) **internal links the model writes in its replies** (e.g. "[the backlog](/projects/11)") rendered as `<a href target="_blank">` ŌĆö a hard navigation/new-tab that remounts the provider tree and resets `open` to its `useState(false)` default (the system prompt tells the model to prefer `navigate_to`, but it frequently emits markdown links anyway); (2) any hard reload / external deep-link entry, since `open` lived only in volatile React state. Fix: `ChatMessageContent`'s link renderer now routes same-origin paths through the Next router client-side (honouring modifier-clicks for new-tab) so the persistent drawer stays mounted, and `BrainContextProvider` persists `open` + `activeChatId` to **sessionStorage** (per-tab; SSR-safe rehydrate-on-mount to avoid a hydration mismatch) so the drawer reopens on its exact conversation after any remount. Covered by `BrainContext.test.tsx` (persist/rehydrate open, resume active chat, honour a manual close). Together with the 2026-06-14 run-store hoist, the Brain now survives **every** navigation, not just its own tool-driven hops.
- **Brain reused the streaming bubble and erased a turn's narration ŌĆö FIXED 2026-06-14 (`brain-embedded/brainRunStore.ts` + `useBrainConversation.ts`).** The agent tool-loop streamed every model turn into one shared `streamingText` buffer that the UI rendered as a single trailing bubble; a turn that narrated *and* called a tool showed its text only transiently, then the next iteration cleared the buffer and reused the same bubble ŌĆö erasing what the user just read (only the final answer was ever persisted). Fix: each turn that produces visible text now persists as its own durable message block, delivered to mounted views as the full run-appended list (merged by id) so React's coalescing of the rapid mid-run emits can't drop the intermediate narration turns. Pure tool-call turns with no text persist nothing. Covered by two new tests in `useBrainConversation.test.tsx`.
- **Brain rendered inline `<tool_call>ŌĆ”</tool_call>` markup as text AND never ran the call ŌĆö FIXED 2026-06-14 (`brain-embedded/src/xmlToolCalls.ts` (new) + `streamChatCompletion.ts`).** `streamChatCompletion` only parsed native OpenAI-structured `tool_calls` deltas; models that emit calls inline in the content stream as `<tool_call>delete_task<arg_key>id</arg_key><arg_value>75</arg_value></tool_call>` had that markup shown verbatim in the bubble ŌĆö and, worse, the call **never executed** (the agent loop only runs structured `toolCalls`), so the Brain "said" it deleted #75 but did nothing. Fix: a streaming-safe `XmlToolCallFilter` lifts inline calls into the same `AssembledToolCall` shape (coercing arg types, so `id` ŌåÆ `75` not `"75"`), strips the markup from the visible/persisted text, and is robust to tags split across stream chunks; native deltas still take precedence. Covered by `xmlToolCalls.test.ts` (8 cases) + a streaming integration test in `streamChatCompletion.test.ts`.
- **Brain run-store cells were session-lived in memory with no eviction ŌĆö FIXED 2026-06-14 (`brain-embedded/src/brainRunStore.ts`).** Hoisting the agent loop out of React (so a run survives navigation) moved each chat's rich transcript + trace + appended-message list from per-instance refs (freed on unmount) into a module-level `Map` keyed by chatId that lived for the whole browser session ŌĆö so a long session touching many chats grew client memory unbounded. Fix: the `Map` is now an LRU bounded to `MAX_CELLS` (50), evicting least-recently-used **idle** cells (never an in-flight run, a cell with a mounted subscriber, or the cell just created for a mounting view); a re-visited evicted chat rebuilds its cell and reloads visible history from persistence (same grounding loss as a page reload). Per-cell, the trace (`MAX_TRACE_EVENTS` 500) and the live-append buffer (`MAX_APPENDED` 50, via shared `recordAppended`) are also capped so a single marathon chat stays bounded. Covered by `brainRunStore.test.ts` (cap, subscriber-protection, LRU recency).

#### ­¤ÅĘ’ĖÅ CoderClaw ŌåÆ BuilderForce rebrand (15)

- **Broken image assets from the rename are now FIXED (frontend).** Root cause: the file sweep
  excluded binary extensions, so `.png` *references* got rebranded but the *files* didn't ŌĆö
  `/claw.png`ŌåÆ`/agentHost.png` (11 refs) and `coderclaw.png`ŌåÆ`/agents.png` (2 refs on `/agents`)
  pointed at non-existent files (404 in prod; the report showed a `522` on `/agentHost.png`, but that
  `522` is Cloudflare-can't-reach-origin ŌĆö a **deploy/infra** issue, separate from the missing file).
  Fix: renamed `public/claw.png`ŌåÆ`agentHost.png`, restored `coderclaw.png` as `public/agents.png`,
  fixed `public/sw.js` precache + bumped its cache `v1`ŌåÆ`v2`. All `src` asset refs now resolve;
  docs-site + agent-runtime/ui were checked and have no `claw`/`agent*` image-ref breakage. CAUTION
  for future asset sweeps: an image is only "dead" if NO reference (including its *renamed* form)
  resolves to it ŌĆö I briefly mis-deleted `coderclaw.png` before realising `/agents.png` was its
  orphaned reference, and recovered it from `git show HEAD:`.

- **`frontend/public/install.ps1` crash + stale URLs FIXED; deeper connect-agent flow mismatch LOGGED.**
  Root cause (again): the rename sweep covered `frontend/src` but **not `frontend/public/`**, so
  `install.ps1` still had `worker.coderclaw.ai` (dead) as its default `$ApiUrl` and `coderclaw.ai`
  in docs. Worse, it called `exit` on failure ŌĆö and the Workforce "Connect a new agent" one-liner
  runs it via `iwr | iex` (in-process), where `exit` **terminates the user's PowerShell session**
  (the reported "crash"). Fixed: URLs ŌåÆ `api.builderforce.ai`/`builderforce.ai`, and every `exit N`
  ŌåÆ `return` so a failure ends the script without killing the host shell.

- **Connect-a-new-agent flow REWRITTEN end-to-end (was: install.ps1 ignored the token).** `install.ps1`
  was a *marketplace-agent registry browser* ŌĆö it ignored `$env:BUILDERFORCE_TOKEN` /
  `$env:BUILDERFORCE_WORKSPACE` and never registered the machine. Rewrote it to: preflight Node/npm ŌåÆ
  `npm i -g @seanhogg/builderforce-agents` ŌåÆ `builderforce connect` ŌåÆ `builderforce gateway`. Added a
  **new headless `builderforce connect`** command ([builderforce-connect.ts](agent-runtime/src/commands/builderforce-connect.ts),
  [register.connect.ts](agent-runtime/src/cli/program/register.connect.ts)) that reads the token from
  env, `POST`s `/api/agent-hosts`, writes the link key to `~/.builderforce/.env`
  (`BUILDERFORCE_API_KEY`/`URL`) and the host id into project context (which the gateway reads to
  connect). tsgo clean. **Prerequisite to actually run:** `@seanhogg/builderforce-agents` must be
  **published to npm** (still blocked ŌĆö `npm whoami` 401); until then step 2 of install.ps1 404s
  (handled gracefully).

- **RuntimeŌåöserver WIRE CONTRACT was split by the rebrand and is now realigned (the real flow break).**
  The product rename used `claw`ŌåÆ`agentNode` but the API uses `claw`ŌåÆ`agent_host`, so the two halves
  of the SAME wire contract diverged. Fixed in `agent-runtime/src`: **API paths** `/api/agentNodesŌĆ”`
  ŌåÆ `/api/agent-hostsŌĆ”` (35 occurrences, 20 files ŌĆö registration/heartbeat/forward/sync/relay/cron/
  skills/personas all were 404ing); **headers** `X-AgentNode-*` ŌåÆ `X-AgentHost-*` (9, matches the
  server's `X-AgentHost-From/Id/Signature`); **registration response** `res.agentNode` ŌåÆ
  `res.agentHost` (server returns `{agentHost, apiKey}`). tsgo clean. **REMAINING audit (logged):**
  other JSON body fields still carry runtime-side names ŌĆö `fromAgentNodeId`/`callbackAgentNodeId`
  (forward), assignment-context, etc. in [api-contract.ts](agent-runtime/src/infra/api-contract.ts) ŌĆö
  each must be verified against its server endpoint's field names; not swept blindly to avoid new
  mismatches. Also `workforce-agent.ts` reads `BUILDERFORCE_AGENTS_LINK_API_KEY` while the rest of the
  runtime uses `BUILDERFORCE_API_KEY` ŌĆö align to one.

- **The "coderclaw" still visible on `/workforce` was DATA, not code** ŌĆö the tenant/workgroup row
  (`tenants.id=1`) was literally named/slugged `coderclaw`. `frontend/src` has **0** `coderclaw`
  refs; the page interpolates the workgroup name. Renamed the tenant ŌåÆ `name='BuilderForce'`,
  `slug='builderforce'` (0 `agent_hosts` referenced it, so the slug change was safe) and added a
  `(workspace)` indicator next to the name in `TopBar.tsx`. Remaining `coderclaw` in `api/src` (7)
  are comments + intentional back-compat (GitHub dispatch label, `coderclawllm/` model-id prefix).

- **Two CI failures from the rebrand are now FIXED + verified** (root cause: `tsc`/`tsgo` were used
  as the local gate, but they don't run the checks CI does). (1) **Frontend** ŌĆö `blogData.ts`
  imported `@/content/blog/agents-and-agent-integration.md` while the renamed file is
  `builderforce-agents-and-agent-integration.md`; `tsc` can't resolve vite's markdown-alias imports
  so it slipped through. Fixed the import; full `vitest run` now green (17 files / 153 tests).
  (2) **API `npm run check:schema`** ŌĆö `check-schema-drift.mjs` statically parsed only `CREATE TABLE`
  / `ADD COLUMN`, so it couldn't follow migration 0078's dynamic `DO`-block `claw`ŌåÆ`agent_host`
  renames and flagged 21 `agent_host_*` columns/tables as "uncreated". My first instinct (grandfather
  the 21) was WRONG ŌĆö that masks drift instead of proving schema.ts matches the migrations. **Proper
  fix shipped:** made the checker **rename-aware** ŌĆö it now follows explicit `ALTER ŌĆ” RENAME TO` /
  `RENAME COLUMN` statements AND declarative `-- @schema-drift-rename-table` /
  `-- @schema-drift-rename-replace` directives (added to 0078, comments only ŌĆö execution unchanged,
  since the dynamic loop is more complete than any explicit list). The 16 migration-created `claw_id`
  columns + 4 workspace tables now **resolve through the rename (NOT grandfathered)**; only the genuine
  baseline-push (`drizzle-kit push`) items remain grandfathered (93, down from the masking 106). `npm
  test` green (schema check + 350 tests). **Lesson:** the real gates are `npm test` (api),
  `pnpm test`/`vitest run` (frontend), `pnpm build` (agent-runtime) ŌĆö not just type checks.

- **Migration 0078 is APPLIED + verified live** (`npm run db:migrate`, 2026-06-03): the configured

#### ­¤ö¦ Engine & runtime consolidation (2)

- **Ō£ģ V1 RETIRED (operator decision executed 2026-06-13) ŌĆö `builderforce-v2` is the consolidated default on every surface; V1 is no longer creatable or default.** Implemented + `tsc` 0 across all 4 packages: (1) `DEFAULT_ENGINE_ID` = `ENGINE_IDS.v2` in [`@builderforce/agent-tools` engine.ts](packages/agent-tools/src/engine.ts) ŌĆö ONE constant flips the on-prem relay `resolveEngine`, cloud `resolveCloudAgent`, `workforceRoutes` create-default, and the `task.assign` fallback together; (2) on-prem **`runV1Engine` DELETED** + its `resolveEngine` registry entry removed ([builderforce-relay.ts](agent-runtime/src/infra/builderforce-relay.ts)) ŌĆö a legacy `engine:"builderforce-v1"` now falls through to v2; (3) **creation restricted to v2** ŌĆö `AGENT_ENGINES = ['builderforce-v2']` ([workforceRoutes.ts](api/src/presentation/routes/workforceRoutes.ts)) + frontend `AgentEngine` narrowed to `'builderforce-v2'` (api.ts/types.ts/CloudAgentFormFields/SlideOutPanel/platformActions); (4) **migration [0120_engine_v2_retire_v1.sql](api/migrations/0120_engine_v2_retire_v1.sql)** back-fills legacy `ide_agents.engine` v1ŌåÆv2 + flips the column default (was v1 in 0087). KEY finding: `builderforce-local` is **on-prem-only** (frontend/api accept only v1|v2), so the prior PRD "flip default ŌåÆ builderforce-local" plan would have BROKEN cloud ŌĆö `builderforce-v2` is the only valid cross-surface engine. **Remaining V1-retirement tail (deploy-gated / dead-code):** (a) the **cloud V1 dispatch branch** still exists as now-unreachable runtime code ŌĆö the `isV2 === false` else-path in [runtimeRoutes.ts](api/src/presentation/routes/runtimeRoutes.ts) (~L430) + `cloudAgentTypeLabel`'s V1 arm; removing it needs cloud tracing + a deploy to verify; (b) **dormant on-prem dead code** ŌĆö `pendingTaskRun` + `flushPendingTaskChanges` (only `runV1Engine` set `pendingTaskRun`; reads are null-guarded so harmless, but now unreachable-for-purpose ŌĆö clean up); (c) **migration 0120 must be applied** (live DB) + a **live e2e** confirming new agents run on V2; (d) README "V1 Cloud Agent" agent-type docs (┬¦ near L854) + migration 0087 header are now historical. **(e) OPEN QUESTION the cutover exposed ŌĆö is `builderforce-local` now dead?** Creation is v2-only and the default `builderforce-v2` = the Claude-Agent-SDK runner (`runV2Engine`), so no agent carries `engine:"builderforce-local"` ŌåÆ the relay's `local` entry + `runLocalEngine` + the entire on-prem `LocalAgentEngine`/`@builderforce/agent-tools` Node engine are unselectable. Two readings of "V2" collide (literal `builderforce-v2`=Claude SDK vs the parity-plan's "surface-agnostic V2 engine"=the shared-registry `LocalAgentEngine`). Operator must pick: (a) confirm Claude-SDK-V2 canonical on-prem ŌåÆ DELETE `builderforce-local`/`runLocalEngine`/the Node `LocalAgentEngine` as dead code (codebase reduction; discards the ┬¦5.2 `local` wins), OR (b) route on-prem through `local` and make Claude-SDK the cloud-only path ŌåÆ make `local` selectable. See PRD ┬¦5.5. Fixing unblocks: a single, unambiguous on-prem engine with zero unreferenced engine code.

- **Ō£ģ RESOLVED 2026-06-13 ŌĆö `agent-runtime` `tsc --noEmit` is now GREEN (0 errors), and the `loadJsonFile` syncŌåÆasync drift is fully propagated.** The root cause was [json-file.ts](agent-runtime/src/infra/json-file.ts) `loadJsonFile` being made `async` (returning `Promise<unknown>`) without updating its synchronous callers (plus a missing `os` import in [subagent-registry.store.ts](agent-runtime/src/agents/subagent-registry.store.ts)). Per the operator directive ("make it all async", not sync), `loadJsonFile` was KEPT async and `await` was propagated through the ENTIRE auth/credential/model subsystem: the auth-profile store loaders (`loadAuthProfileStore`/`loadAuthProfileStoreForAgent`/`ensureAuthProfileStore`/`updateAuthProfileStoreWithLock`), the external-CLI credential readers ([cli-credentials.ts](agent-runtime/src/agents/cli-credentials.ts) ŌĆö Claude/Codex/Qwen/MiniMax read+cached + the file-write path) and `syncExternalCliCredentials`, the subagent registry read path (`getRunsSnapshotForRead` ŌåÆ `findRunIdsByChildSessionKey`/`resolveRequesterForChildSession`/`countActiveRunsForSession`/`countActiveDescendantRuns`/`listDescendantRunsForRequester`/`isSubagentSessionRunActive`/`markSubagentRunTerminated`, and their callers in subagent-announce/spawn/tools, auto-reply abort, and the cron isolated-agent runner), the telegram sticker cache, and the model-auth hub (`resolveApiKeyForProvider`/`resolveModelAuthMode`/`resolveModelAuthLabel`/`normalizeProviders`/`resolveModelSelectionFromDirective`/`createProviderAuthChecker`/`resolveImageModelConfigForTool` + their consumers across `commands/*`, `provider-usage.auth.ts`, `directive-handling.*`, `status.ts`, `model-picker.ts`, `model-fallback.ts`). Sync-contract sites were handled structurally: the `image` tool factory stays SYNC (it runs in the synchronous tool-assembly) and resolves its model config lazily inside the async `execute`; the model-picker auth predicate stays a sync `(provider)=>boolean` over a store preloaded by its now-async factory. Verified: `agent-runtime` `tsc --noEmit` exits 0 (production + tests). **Corrected 2026-06-13 (this pass):** the same drift had survived in [github-copilot-token.ts](agent-runtime/src/providers/github-copilot-token.ts) ŌĆö its injectable `loadJsonFileImpl`/`saveJsonFileImpl` seams were typed SYNC (`=> unknown` / `=> void`) while their defaults are the now-async `loadJsonFile`/`saveJsonFile`, and the call sites did NOT `await`. tsc stayed green because `Promise<unknown>` is assignable to `unknown`, so the type masked the bug: in production the cache read returned a `Promise`, `cached.token` was always `undefined`, the valid cache was never honored, and a fresh token was fetched on every call (the save was a fire-and-forget write). Fixed by widening the seams to `=> unknown | Promise<unknown>` / `=> void | Promise<void>` and `await`ing both calls ŌĆö and a regression test now exercises an async (Promise-returning) loader and asserts the cache is honored. **Residual:** behavioral test execution (vitest) across the OTHER changed credential/subagent/model-auth paths was NOT run in this pass (type-safety verified, but the syncŌåÆasync semantics change warrants a full `pnpm test` run on agent-runtime before release).

#### ­¤öÉ Multi-tenant, governance & embed (3)

- **[ACCEPTED BY DESIGN 2026-05-31] Identity federation uses a shared-secret HS256 token, not OIDC issuer verification (spec ┬¦2.1 + ┬¦7 item 1).** [JwtService.verifyJwt](api/src/infrastructure/auth/JwtService.ts) verifies an HMAC-SHA-256 signature against a single shared `JWT_SECRET`; the federation token carries no `iss` claim and [authMiddleware](api/src/presentation/middleware/authMiddleware.ts) does no issuer/`tenants.idp_issuer` check. The spec's wording (BurnRateOS as an OIDC IdP verified by asymmetric issuer + signature) is **intentionally not implemented**: BurnRateOS and BuilderForce are first-party apps with a co-managed secret, so the symmetric model is accepted. Residual risk acknowledged (a secret leak lets either side forge the other's tokens; no cryptographic IdP boundary; `persona`/`plan` claims absent, so plan-based gating falls back to `role` + the segment's `plan`). Revisit only if a non-first-party host ever federates in ŌĆö then move to RS256/JWKS keyed by the already-present `tenants.idp_issuer` column. No code change this pass.

- **Segment tier foundation + write-isolation + provisioning ŌĆö LANDED ([0054](api/migrations/0054_segment_tier.sql), [0056](api/migrations/0056_segment_id_propagation.sql), [segmentResolver](api/src/infrastructure/auth/segmentResolver.ts), [segmentRoutes](api/src/presentation/routes/segmentRoutes.ts)).** Shipped + applied + verified: the `segments` table + tenant `kind`/`idp_issuer`/`isolation_mode`/`settings` columns + one default segment per tenant (0054); `segment_id` (NOT NULL in DB, optional in TS) on 34 business tables + `tasks` via project, backfilled to each tenant's default (0056); a DB-level default-fill trigger that auto-stamps the default segment for `single` tenants and RAISEs for `segmented` tenants (the no-bleed hard rule enforced at the DB ŌĆö verified: single fills, segmented rejects); `resolveSegment()` chokepoint (default for single, lazy-create from account/company claims for segmented, cached) wired into [authMiddleware](api/src/presentation/middleware/authMiddleware.ts) setting `c.get('segmentId')`; and `GET/POST/PATCH /api/segments` provisioning. Unit + full suite green (108 tests). **Still open** ŌĆö see the four bullets below.

- **[FOOT-GUN FIXED 2026-06-13 ŌĆö operator env-set remains] `NEXT_PUBLIC_EMBED_ALLOWED_HOST_ORIGINS` must be set in prod to enable embedding.** The single allowlist drives both the `/embed/*` `frame-ancestors` CSP (middleware) and the client-side auth-origin check ([useEmbedFrame](frontend/src/lib/embed/useEmbedFrame.ts)). **The default-OPEN foot-gun is closed:** the trust decision was extracted to the pure [isTrustedHostOrigin](frontend/src/lib/embed/embedTrust.ts) (+unit tests) and the frame is now **default-CLOSED in production** when the allowlist is empty (rejects all origins, mirroring the `frame-ancestors 'self'` CSP so both layers fail the same way), while staying open in dev for cross-origin convenience. **Residual (operator):** an empty allowlist in prod now blocks embedding entirely (safe but non-functional) ŌĆö so to actually *enable* embedding the env must be set to the BurnRateOS origins per environment. No code change available for the env-set.

- **Ō£ģ COMPLETED 2026-06-14 ŌĆö installer env wiring done on both OSes.** [install.ps1](frontend/public/install.ps1) already read `BUILDERFORCE_TOKEN`/`BUILDERFORCE_URL` and ran `builderforce connect` (rebrand/connect pass). - **Ō£ģ COMPLETED 2026-06-14 ŌĆö cold-invite email shipped.** The pending-invite branch of `POST /api/tenants/:id/invite-by-email` ([tenantRoutes.ts](api/src/presentation/routes/tenantRoutes.ts)) now sends a `sendWorkspaceInviteEmail` ([EmailService.ts](api/src/infrastructure/email/EmailService.ts), Resend, best-effort ŌĆö no-ops without `RESEND_API_KEY`): it names the inviter + workspace + role and links to `/register?email=<invited>` so the pending `tenant_invitations` row auto-converts on first login. api `tsc` 0. They only "land" if they independently sign up with the same email. Fixing (send an invite email with a signup link on the pending path, and/or surface "you've been invited to N workspaces" on the tenant picker) unblocks: true cold invites to people who don't already use the product.

- **Ō£ģ RESOLVED 2026-06-14 ŌĆö superseded by the `workflow_triggers` webhook transport (no new code).** A data-collection trigger that must receive an inbound payload is configured as `triggerType:'webhook'`, which mints a per-trigger token (`workflow_triggers.token`) + a public `POST /api/workflow-triggers/hook/:token` ([workflowTriggerRoutes.ts](api/src/presentation/routes/workflowTriggerRoutes.ts), HMAC-verified via `X-Signature`) that `instantiateWorkflowRun` fires with the posted body as the trigger node output ŌĆö exactly this gapŌĆÖs capability, via a per-trigger-node token (better than the per-definition token originally proposed). Labels with no autonomous transport (form-submit/signup/purchase/ŌĆ”) stay manual-only by design ([workflowTriggers.ts](api/src/domain/workflowTriggers.ts)). Building `/api/ingest/:token` would have duplicated it. ORIGINAL GAP: **Inbound data-collection ingest endpoint is not implemented ŌĆö marketing triggers can't actually fire.** Data-collection trigger types (form-submit, webhook, page-view, signup, purchase, email-open/click, rss, inbound-email) and trigger integrations (Typeform, Stripe, Segment, ŌĆ”) are configurable + persist + compile, but there is no public HTTP endpoint that RECEIVES an inbound payload and starts a run. Needs a per-definition ingest token (column on `workflow_definitions` + migration), a default agent-host for the run, and a public `POST /api/ingest/:token` route that seeds the trigger node's output with the posted body and instantiates a run (reusing the `/run` compile path). Fixing unblocks: workflows that genuinely fire from collected marketing data (the "marketing platform with triggers" use case).

#### ­¤¦╣ Quality & token-cost (1)

- **Token-cost pass ŌĆö VERIFIED NOT BUGS (do not re-audit):** Two claims from the first-pass review were refuted on direct inspection. (a) *agent-runtime "doesn't enable Anthropic caching"* ŌĆö false: [config/defaults.ts](agent-runtime/src/config/defaults.ts) force-defaults `cacheRetention: "short"` on every Anthropic model (and the primary) under `api_key` auth, which flows through `applyExtraParamsToAgent` ŌåÆ `resolveCacheRetention` ŌåÆ pi-ai `streamSimple`'s `cacheRetention` stream option (which applies the `cache_control` breakpoint). Caching is ON by default. (b) *gateway "strips `cache_control`"* ŌĆö false: messages are forwarded verbatim ([LlmProxyService.dispatch](api/src/application/llm/LlmProxyService.ts) casts `messages` through and [openrouter buildBody](api/src/application/llm/vendors/openrouter.ts) passes them untouched; [sanitizeRequestToolNames](api/src/application/llm/toolNameSanitizer.ts) spreads `{...m}` preserving `content`). `cache_control` is nested in `messages[].content[]`, not a top-level field, so `stripStandardFields` never touches it. Tenant-set caching survives the proxy today.

Fixing (optionally hard-gate Run behind a passing check, and synthesize a minimal tsconfig for the fallback) unblocks: a true "code must be good before it runs" gate.

- **Ō£ģ RESOLVED 2026-06-14 (T2).** `Select.tsx` gains native-style keyboard type-ahead (buffer + startsWith/substring, commit-on-match); residual = drop now-defensive-only `select` color-scheme CSS. - **`/llm/v1/messages` plan daily-token cap ŌĆö RESOLVED (2026-06-14, T3).** The our-models branch (no tenant Anthropic key ŌåÆ served from OUR pool, billing US) previously skipped the `llmUsageLog`-SUM daily-cap gate that `/v1/chat/completions` enforced. - **Cache-read tokens charged at full weight in the daily-cap ledger ŌĆö RESOLVED (2026-06-14, T3).** The plan daily-limit gate summed `total_tokens` at 1├Ś, ignoring the cache-read/creation discount that `computeCostMillicents` already applied to *cost*. The shared `enforceDailyTokenCap` helper now sums a cache-discounted effective total (`SUM(total_tokens ŌłÆ 0.9┬Ęcache_read + 0.25┬Ęcache_creation)`) via `CACHE_READ_MULTIPLIER`/`CACHE_CREATION_MULTIPLIER` exported from [usageLedger.ts](api/src/application/llm/usageLedger.ts), so tenants get the cached-input discount in their *budget* and the `x-builderforce-daily-tokens-*` headers ŌĆö not just in the log. tsc 0 + tests.

- **Ō£ģ RESOLVED 2026-06-14 (T5).** `saveAuthProfileStore`+`ensureAuthStoreFile` made `async` with `await` propagated through all ~10 call sites + 3 test files ŌĆö durable, ordered credential writes; closes the last json-file sync/async seam. ORIGINAL GAP: **The auth-profile WRITE path still fires the async `saveJsonFile` without `await` (pre-existing ŌĆö `saveJsonFile` has always been async, so NOT part of the `loadJsonFile` syncŌåÆasync fix).** [`saveAuthProfileStore`](agent-runtime/src/agents/auth-profiles/store.ts#L336) and [`ensureAuthStoreFile`](agent-runtime/src/agents/auth-profiles/paths.ts#L24) are declared SYNC (`: void`) yet call the async `saveJsonFile`, making every credential/auth-store write a fire-and-forget Promise: a write failure becomes an unhandled rejection (process-level crash risk under `unhandledRejection`), and a caller that reads the store back immediately after can race the not-yet-flushed write. Left sync this pass to avoid a wide cascade ŌĆö making them async forces `await` through ~10 production call sites (oauth.ts, usage.ts, profiles.ts, store.ts) plus ~6 test files, and re-exports via `auth-profiles.ts`. Fixing (make both functions `async`, `await saveJsonFile`, and propagate `await` to every caller per the operator "make it all async" directive) unblocks: durable, ordered credential writes with no unhandled-rejection surface ŌĆö closing the last `json-file` sync/async seam.

- **Ō£ģ RESOLVED (T6, 2026-06-14) ŌĆö the noise-level-scaled bias formula shipped; latent-residual coherence now composes with img2img.** The binary skip-gate `shouldApplyLatentResidualBias` was replaced by [`latentResidualBiasScale`](Builderforce.ai/studio/src/engine/mamba-coherence.ts), which returns the multiplier `applyToLatent` (now takes a `noiseScale` param) applies to its per-channel offset: `1` on the fresh-noise path, `sqrt(1-ßŠ▒_t)` under img2img ŌĆö so the bias perturbs only the noise component and leaves the carried-forward signal intact. The schedule's noise fraction comes from the new `DiffusionEngine.noiseScaleForTimestep` (single source of truth, also now backing `addNoiseToLatent`); `video-engine.ts` `produceClip` wires it. Unit-tested in [mamba-coherence.test.ts](Builderforce.ai/studio/src/engine/mamba-coherence.test.ts) (bias-scale gate + proportional-offset + no-op). ORIGINAL GAP follows. [studio/src/engine/mamba-coherence.ts `shouldApplyLatentResidualBias`](studio/src/engine/mamba-coherence.ts) gates the bias and returns `false` whenever `useImg2Img` is on (the bug it fixes: `applyToLatent` adds a per-channel broadcast constant designed for unit-variance noise, which catastrophically disfigures partially-denoised img2img latents and compounds frame-to-frame). The conservative fix means a user picking `latent-residual` + `imgToImgStrength > 0` gets the same temporal coherence behaviour as `prompt-bias` + img2img (i.e. zero latent-side Mamba bias). A proper fix would scale the bias by the schedule noise level ŌĆö at timestep `t` the latent is `sqrt(╬▒)┬Ęclean + sqrt(1-╬▒)┬Ęnoise`, so scaling the broadcast bias by `sqrt(1-╬▒)` would perturb only the noise portion and leave the signal intact, letting both mechanisms compose. Fixing (one parameter on `applyToLatent`, one call site, one test) unblocks: stacking trained-state coherence on top of img2img for the longer-clip "scene-aware walking" use case.

- **Ō£ģ RESOLVED (T6, 2026-06-14) ŌĆö the silent contradiction is gone.** The scattered `showAdvanced ? model : tier.primary` ternaries were unified into one source of truth, [`resolveEffectiveChain`](Builderforce.ai/studio-embedded/src/components/QualityTierPicker.tsx) (used by the engine factory, saved-version params, the debug snapshot, and the badge). A self-contained [`EffectiveChainBadge`](Builderforce.ai/studio-embedded/src/components/QualityTierPicker.tsx) renders the authoritative effective chain and flags when Advanced has overridden the tier; the Quality picker is now `disabled` while an Advanced override is active, so both surfaces can no longer claim to be in effect at once. ORIGINAL GAP follows. When the user opens Advanced and picks a specific model, the engine uses *that* model and skips the refinement pass even if Quality is set to "Refined" ([StudioPanel.tsx](studio-embedded/src/components/StudioPanel.tsx) ŌĆö the `showAdvanced ? model : tier.primary` ternary). The current Quality picker doesn't visually indicate it was overridden, so a user with Advanced open + Refined selected sees both controls active and the tier description (lying about "two-pass chain") while only single-pass runs. Fixing (either grey out the Quality picker when Advanced model is set, or grey out the Advanced model picker when Quality !== "fast/balanced/refined", with a single resolved-state badge showing the effective model chain) unblocks: no silent contradiction between the two control surfaces.

- **Ō£ģ RESOLVED 2026-06-14 (T7).** `emitWebhookEvent` persists the signed body; non-2xx/network failures retry via capped backoff (5ŌåÆ10ŌåÆ20ŌåÆ40ŌåÆ80m, max 6 then dead-letter) in a `scheduled()` sweep re-signing under the original delivery-id nonce (idempotent). Migration 0160. - **Ō£ģ RESOLVED 2026-06-14 (T8).** new `awaiting_workflow` lifecycle + `ticket_runs.awaiting_workflow_id` (migration 0171) parks the ticket; a poll sweep (`resumeParkedWorkflows`) advances on settle / routes to `needs_attention` on fail/missing-definition. Fixing (a back-edge that parks the ticket until the spawned workflow settles and maps its status onto the ticket lifecycle, plus surfacing a missing-definition error instead of a silent no-op) unblocks: lane actions that genuinely gate on a downstream workflow's outcome.

- **Ō£ģ RESOLVED 2026-06-14 (T8).** `runBoardSyncSweep` (wired into `scheduled()`) honors each active connectionŌĆÖs `poll_interval_sec` and runs `syncConnection`+`drainOutbox` with per-connection failure isolation. - **Ō£ģ RESOLVED 2026-06-14 (T8).** JSONB `fields` column (migration 0170); `upsertLink` writes it and `getLink` reads it back ŌĆö unblocks field-level three-way merge.
